You see , he know that he have find the place where Granny be in the habit of take a sun-nap .

Yes , indeed , I think we will give you a surprise .

CHAPTER VII : Granny Fox Has A Bad Dream Nothing ever simply happen ; Bear that point in mind .
If you look long and hard enough A cause you 'll always find .
-- Old Granny Fox .
Old Granny Fox be dream .
Yes , Sir , she be dream .

Oh ! ''

CHAPTER VIII : What Farmer Brown 's Boy Did In time of danger heed this rule : Think hard and fast , but pray keep cool .
-- Old Granny Fox .

CHAPTER IX : Reddy Fox Hears About Granny Fox Though you may think another wrong And be quite positive you 're right , Do n't let your temper get away ; And try at least to be polite .

CHAPTER X : Reddy Fox Is Impudent A saucy tongue be dangerous to possess ; Be sure some day ' t will get you in a mess .
-- Old Granny Fox .

She have allow Farmer Brown 's boy to catch her napping !
Reddy do wish he have be there to see it himself .

Reddy do a thing no truly wise Fox ever will do .

CHAPTER XI : After The Storm The joy and the sunshine that make u glad ; The worry and trouble that make u sad Must come to an end ; so why complain Of too little sun or too much rain ?
-- Old Granny Fox .
The thing to do be to make the most of the sunshine while it last , and when it rain to look forward to the corning of the sun again , know that conic it surely will .
A dreadful storm be keep the little people of the Green Forest , the Green Meadows , and the Old Orchard prisoner in their own home or in such place of shelter a they have be able to find .
But it could n't last forever , and they know it .
Knowing this be all that keep some of them alive .
You see , they be starve .
Yes , Sir , they be starve .
You and I would be very hungry , very hungry indeed , if we have to go without food for two whole day , but if we be snug and warm it would n't do u any real harm .
With the little wild friend , especially the little feathered folk , it be a very different matter .
You see , they be naturally so active that they have to fill their stomachs very often in order to supply their little body with heat and energy .
So when their food supply be wholly cut off , they starve or else freeze to death in a very short time .
A great many little life be end this way in every long , hard winter storm .
It be late in the afternoon of the second day when rough Brother North Wind decide that he have show his strength and fierceness long enough , and rumble and grumble retire from the Green Meadows and the Green Forest , blow the snow cloud away with him .
For just a little while before it be time for him to go to bed behind the Purple Hills , jolly , round , red Mr. Sun smile down on the white land , and never be his smile more welcome .
Out from their shelter hurry all the little prisoner , for they must make the most of the short time before the come of the cold night .
Little Tommy Tit the Chickadee be so weak that he could hardly fly , and he shake with chill .
He make straight for the apple-tree where Farmer Brown 's boy always keep a piece of suet tie to a branch for Tommy and his friend .
Drummer the Woodpecker be there before him .
Now it be one of the law of politeness among the feathered folk that when one be eat from a piece of suet a newcomer shall await his turn .
`` Dee , dee , dee ! ''
say Tommy Tit faintly but cheerfully , for he could n't be other than cheery if he try .
`` Dee , dee , dee !
That look good to me . ''

Do n't wait for me , for I wo n't be through for a long time .
I 'm nearly starve , and I guess you must be . ''
`` I be , '' confess Tommy , a he fly over beside Drummer .
`` Thank you ever so much for not make me wait . ''
`` Do n't mention it , '' reply Drummer , with his mouth full .
`` This be no time for politeness .
Here come Yank Yank the Nuthatch .
I guess there be room for him too . ''
Yank Yank be promptly invite to join them and do so after apologize for seem so greedy .
`` If I could n't get my stomach full before night , I certainly should freeze to death before morning , '' say he .

If I have to hunt for my usual food on the tree , I certainly should have to give up and die .

My , I feel like a new bird already !
Here come Sammy Jay .
I wonder if he will try to drive u away a he usually do . ''
Sammy do nothing of the kind .
He be very meek and most polite .

he ask .
`` I would n't ask it but that I could n't last another night without food . ''
`` Dee , dee , dee !
Always room for one more , '' reply Tommy Tit , crowd over to give Sammy room .

As he flounder through the snow to another apple-tree he saw Tommy Tit and his friend , and in his heart he rejoice that they have find food wait for them .
His own trouble be at an end , for in the tree he be head for be a store of corn .
CHAPTER XII : Granny And Reddy Fox Hunt In Vain Old Mother Nature 's plan for good Quite often be not understood .
-- Old Granny Fox .
Tommy Tit and Drummer the Woodpecker and Yank Yank the Nuthatch and Sammy Jay and Chatterer the Red Squirrel be not the only one who be out and about as soon a the great storm end .
Oh , my , no !
No , indeed !

Peter Rabbit and Mrs. Peter come out of the hole in the heart of the dear Old Briar-patch , where they have manage to keep comfortably warm , and at once begin to fill their stomach with bark from young tree and tender tip of twig .
It be very coarse food , but it would take away that empty feeling .
Mrs. Grouse burst out of the snow and hurry to get a meal before dark .

That seem like a dreadful hope , do n't it ?
But one of the first law of Old Mother Nature be self-preservation .
That mean to save your own life first .
So perhaps Granny and Reddy be not to be blame for hop that some of their neighbor might be catch easily because of the great storm .
They be very hungry indeed , and they could not eat bark like Peter Rabbit , or bud like Mrs. Grouse , or seed like Whitefoot the Woodmouse .
Their teeth and stomach be not make for such food .
It be hard go for Granny and Reddy Fox .
The snow be soft and deep in many place , and they have to keep pretty close to those place where rough Brother North Wind have blow away enough of the snow to make walk fairly easy .

`` We 'll go down to the Old Briar-patch .

Peter Rabbit may take it into his silly head to come outside , '' say Granny , lead the way .
When they reach the dear Old Briar-patch they find that Peter be not outside .
In fact , peer between the bramble and bush , they could see his little brown form bob about a he hunt for tender bark .
He have already make little path along which he could hop easily .
Peter saw them almost as soon a they saw him .
`` Hard time these , '' say Peter pleasantly .
`` I hope your stomach be not as empty a mine . ''
He pull a strip of bark from a young tree and begin to chew it .
This be more than Reddy could stand .
To see Peter eat while his own stomach be just one great big ache from emptiness be too much .
`` I 'm go in there and catch him , or drive him out where you can catch him , if I tear my coat all to piece ! ''
snarl Reddy .
Peter stop chew and sit up .
`` Come right along , Reddy .
Come right along if you want to , but I would advise you to save your skin and your coat , '' say he .
Reddy 's only reply be a snarl a he push his way under the bramble .
He yelp a they tear his coat and scratch his face , but he keep on .
Now Peter 's path be very cunningly make .
He have cut them through the very thick of the briar just big enough for himself and Mrs. Peter to hop along comfortably .
But Reddy be so much big that he have to force his way through and in place crawl flat on his stomach , which be very slow work , to say nothing of the painful scratch from the briar .
It be no trouble at all for Peter to keep out of his way , and before long Reddy give up .
Without a word Granny Fox lead the way to the Green Forest .
They would try to find where Mrs. Grouse be sleep under the snow .
But though they hunt all night , they fail to find her , for she wisely have go to bed in a spruce-tree .
CHAPTER XIII : Granny Fox Admits Growing Old Who will not admit he be old each day fool no one but himself .
-- Old Granny Fox .
Old Granny Fox be a spry old lady for her age .
If you do n't believe it just try to catch her .
But spry a she be , she be n't as spry a she use to be .
No , Sir , Granny Fox be n't as spry a she use to be .
The truth be , Granny be get old .
She never would admit it , and Reddy never have realize it until the day after the great storm .
All that night they have hunt in vain for something to eat and at daylight have creep into their house to rest awhile before start on another hunt .
They have neither the strength nor the courage to search any long then .
Wading through snow be very hard work at best and very tiresome , but when your stomach have be empty for so long that you almost begin to wonder what food taste like , it become hard work still .
You see , it be food that make strength , and lack of food take away strength .
This be why Granny and Reddy Fox just HAD to rest .
Hungry a they be , they HAD to give up for awhile .
Reddy flung himself down , and if ever there be a discouraged young Fox he be that one .
`` I wish I be dead , '' he moan .

`` That 's no way for a young Fox to talk !

I be indeed . ''

It seem very far away .

You know his be a very suspicious nature .
Could it be that Granny have some secret plan of her own to get a meal and want to get rid of him ?
`` What 's the matter with you ? ''
he demand roughly .
`` It be you who propose go over to the Old Pasture . ''

It be a sad sort of smile .
She be wonderfully sharp and smart , be Granny Fox , and she know what be in Reddy 's mind as well a if he have tell her .
`` Old bone do n't rest and recover as quickly a young bone , and I just do n't feel equal to go over there now , '' say she .

I be go to stay right here and rest .

There be something in the way Granny speak that tell Reddy she be speak the truth .
It be the very first time she ever have admit that she be grow old and be no long the equal of any Fox .
Never before have he notice how gray she have grow .
Reddy felt a feeling of shame creep over him , -- shame that he have suspect Granny of play a sharp trick .
And this little feeling of shame be follow instantly by a splendid thought .
He would go out and find food of some kind , and he would bring it straight back to Granny .
He have be take care of by Granny when he be little , and now he would repay Granny for all she have do for him by take care of her in her old age .
`` Go back in the house and lie down , Granny , '' say he kindly .
`` I be go to get something , and whatever it may be you shall have your share . ''
With this he trot off towards the Old Pasture and somehow he do n't mind the ache in his stomach a he have before .
CHAPTER XIV : Three Vain And Foolish Wishes There 's nothing so foolishly silly and vain As to wish for a thing you can never attain .
-- Old Granny Fox .
We all know that , yet most of u be just foolish enough to make such a wish now and then .
I guess you have do it .
I know I have .
Peter Rabbit have do it often and then laugh at himself afterwards .
I suspect that even shrewd , clever old Granny Fox have be guilty of it more than once .
So it be not surprising that Reddy Fox , terribly hungry a he be , should do a little foolish wishing .
When he leave home to go to the Old Pasture , in the hope that he would be able to find something to eat there , he start off bravely .
It be cold , very cold indeed , but his fur coat keep him warm as long a he be move .
The Green Meadows be glisten white with snow .
All the world , at least all that part of it with which Reddy be acquaint , be white .
It be beautiful , very beautiful , a million of sparkle flash in the sun .
But Reddy have no thought for beauty ; the only thought he have room for be to get something to put in the empty stomach of himself and Granny Fox .
Jack Frost have harden the snow so that Reddy no longer have to wade through it .
He could run on the crust now without break through .
This make it much easier , so he trot along swiftly .
He have intend to go straight to the Old Pasture , but there suddenly pop into his head a memory of the shelter down in a far corner of the Old Orchard which Farmer Brown 's boy have build for Bob White .
Probably the Bob White family be there now , and he might surprise them .
He would go there first .
Reddy stop and look carefully to make sure that Farmer Brown 's boy and Bowser the Hound be nowhere in sight .
Then he run swiftly towards the Old Orchard .
Just a he enter it he hear a merry voice just over his head : `` Dee , dee , dee , dee ! ''
Reddy stop and look up .
There be Tommy Tit the Chickadee cling tightly to a big piece of fresh suet tie fast to a branch of a tree , and Tommy be stuff himself .
Reddy sit down right underneath that suet and look up longingly .
The sight of it make his mouth water so that it be almost more than he could stand .
He jump once .
He jump twice .
He jump three time .
But all his jumping be in vain .
That suet be beyond his reach .
There be no possible way of reach it save by fly or climb .
Reddy 's tongue hang out of his mouth with longing .
`` I wish I could climb , '' say Reddy .
But he could n't climb , and all the wishing in the world would n't enable him to , a he very well know .
So after a little he start on .
As he draw near the far corner of the Old Orchard , he saw Bob White and Mrs. Bob and all the young Bobs pick up grain which Farmer Brown 's boy have scatter for them just in front of the shelter he have build for them .
Reddy crouch down and very slowly , an inch at a time , he creep forward , his eye shin with eagerness .
Just a he be almost within spring distance , Bob White give a signal , and away fly the Bob Whites to the safety of a hemlock-tree on the edge of the Green Forest .
Tears of rage and disappointment well up in Reddy 's eye .
`` I wish I could fly , '' he mutter , a he watch the brown bird disappear in the big hemlock-tree .
This be quite a foolish a wish a the other , so Reddy trot on and decide to go down past the Smiling Pool .
When he get there he find it , a he expect , freeze over .
But just where the Laughing Brook join it there be a little place where there be open water .
Billy Mink be on the ice at it edge , and just a Reddy get there Billy dive in .
A minute later he climb out with a fish in his mouth .
`` Give me a bite , '' beg Reddy .
`` Catch your own fish , '' retort Billy Mink .
`` I have to work hard enough for what I get a it be . ''
Reddy be afraid to go out on the ice where Billy be , and so he sit and watch him eat that fine fish .
Then Billy dive into the water again and disappear .
Reddy wait a long time , but Billy do not return .
`` I wish I could dive , '' gulp Reddy , thinking of the fine fish somewhere under the ice .
And this wish be quite as foolish a the other wish .
CHAPTER XV : Reddy Fights A Battle ' T be not the foe that be without But those that be within That give u battle that we find The hard be to win .
-- Old Granny Fox After the last of his three foolish wish , Reddy Fox leave the Smiling Pool and head straight for the Old Pasture for which he have start in the first place .
He wish now that he have go straight there .
Then he would n't have see the suet tie out of reach to the branch of a tree in the Old Orchard ; he would n't have see the Bob Whites fly away to safety just a he felt almost sure of catch one ; he would n't have see Billy Mink bring a fine fish out of the water and eat it right before him .
It be bad enough to be starve with no food in sight , but to be as hungry a Reddy Fox be and to see food just out of reach , to smell it , and not be able to get it be , -- well , it be more than most folk can stand patiently .
So Reddy Fox be grumble to himself a he hurry to the Old Pasture and his heart be very bitter .
It seem to him that everything be against him .
His neighbor have food , but he have none , not so much a a crumb .
It be unfair .
Old Mother Nature be unjust .
If he could climb he could get food .
If he could fly he could get food .
If he could dive he could get food .
But he could neither climb , fly , nor dive .
He do n't stop to think that Old Mother Nature have give him some of the sharp wit in all the Green Forest or on all the Green Meadows ; that she have give him a wonderful nose ; that she have give him the keenest of ear ; that she have give him speed excel by few .
He forget these thing and be so busy think bitterly of the thing he do n't have that he forget to use his wit and nose and ear when he reach the Old Pasture .
The result be that he trot right past Old Jed Thumper , the big gray Rabbit , who be sit behind a little bush hold his breath .
The minute Old Jed saw that Reddy be safely past , he start for his bull-briar castle a fast a he could .
It be not until then that Reddy discover him .
Of course , Reddy start after him , and this time he make good use of his speed .
But he be too late .
Old Jed Thumper reach his castle with Reddy two jump behind him .
Reddy know now that there be no chance to catch Old Jed that day , and for a few minute he felt more bitter than ever .
Then all in a flash Reddy Fox become the shrewd , clever fellow that he really be .
he grin .
`` It 's of no use to try to fill an empty stomach on wish , '' say he .
`` If I have come straight here and mind my own business , I 'd have catch old Jed Thumper .
Now I 'm go to get some food and I 'm not go home until I do . ''
Very wisely Reddy put all unpleasant thought out of his head and settle down to use his wit and his eye and his ear and his nose for all they be worth , a Old Mother Nature have intend he should .
All through the Old Pasture he hunt , take care not to miss a single place where there be the least chance of find food .
But it be all in vain .
Reddy gulp down his disappointment .
`` Now for the Big River , '' say he , and start off bravely .
When he reach the edge of the Big River , he hurry along the bank until he reach a place where the water seldom freeze .
As he have hop , he find that it be not frozen now .
It look so black and cold that it make him shiver just to see it .
Back and forth with his nose to the ground he run .
Suddenly he stop and sniff .
Then he sniff again .
Then he follow his nose straight to the very edge of the Big River .
There , float in the black water , be a dead fish !
By wad in he could get it .
Reddy shiver at the touch of the cold water , but what be wet foot compare with such an empty stomach a his ?
In a minute he have that fish and be back on the shore .
It be n't a very big fish , but it would stop the ache in his stomach until he could get something more .
With a sigh of pure happiness he sink his teeth into it and then -- well , then he remember poor Old Granny Fox .
Reddy swallow a mouthful and try to forget Granny .
But he could n't .
He swallow another mouthful .
Poor old Granny be back there at home as hungry a he be and too stiff and tire to hunt .
Reddy choke .
Then he begin a battle with himself .
His stomach demand that fish .
If he eat it , no one would be the wiser .
But Granny need it even more than he do .
For a long time Reddy fought with himself .
In the end he pick up the fish and start for home .
CHAPTER XVI : Reddy Is Made Truly Happy It 's what you do for others , Not what they do for you , That make you feel so happy All through and through and through .
-- Old Granny Fox .
Reddy Fox run all the way home from the Big River just as fast a he could go .
In his mouth he carry the fish he have find and from which he have take just two bite .
You remember he have have a battle with himself over that fish , and now he be run away from himself .
That sound funny , do n't it ?
But it be true .
Yes , Sir , Reddy Fox be run away from himself .
He be afraid that if he do n't get home to Old Granny Fox with that fish very soon , he would eat every last bit of it himself .
So he be run his very hard so a to get there before this could happen .
So really he be run away from himself , from his selfish self .
Old Granny Fox be on the doorstep watch for him , and he saw just how her hungry old eye brighten when she saw him and what he have .
`` I 've bring you something to eat , Granny , '' he pant , a he lay the fish at her foot .
He be quite out of breath with run .
`` It be n't much , but it be something .
It be all I could find for you . ''
Granny look at the fish and then she look sharply at Reddy , and into those keen yellow eye of hers creep a soft , tender look , such a look a you would never have believe they could have hold .
`` What have YOU have to eat ? ''
ask Granny softly .
Reddy turn his head that Granny might not see his face .
`` Oh , I 've have something , '' say he , try to speak lightly .
It be true ; he have have two bite from that fish .
Now you know just how shrewd and smart and wise Granny Fox be .
Reddy do n't fool her just the least little bit .
She take two small bite from the fish .
`` Now , '' say she , `` we 'll divide it , '' and she bit in two part what remain .
In a twinkling she have gulp down the small part , for you know she be very , very hungry .
`` That be your share , '' say she , a she push what remain over to Reddy .
Reddy try to refuse it .
`` I bring it all for you , '' say he .
`` I know you do , Reddy , '' reply Granny , and it seem to Reddy that he never have know her voice to sound so gentle .
`` You bring it to me when all you have have be the two little bite you have take from it .
You ca n't fool me , Reddy Fox .
There be n't one good meal for either of u in that fish , but there be enough to give u both a little hope and keep u from starve .
Now you mind what I say and eat your share . ''
Granny say this last very sternly .
Reddy look at Granny , and then he bolt down that little piece of fish without another word .
`` That 's good , '' say Granny .
`` We will feel well , both of u .
Now that I 've something in my stomach , I feel two year young .
Before you come , I do n't feel a if I should ever be able to go on another hunt .
If you have n't bring something , I -- I 'm afraid I could n't have last much longer .
By another day you probably would n't have have old Granny to think of .
You may not know it , but I know that you save my life , Reddy .
I have reach a point where I just have to have a little food .
You know there be time when a very little food be of more good than a lot of food could be later .
This be one of those time . ''
Never in all his life have Reddy Fox felt so truly happy .
He be still hungry , -- very , very hungry .
But he give it no thought .
He have save Granny Fox , good old Granny who have teach him all he know .
And he know that Granny know how he have have to fight with himself to do it .
Reddy be happy through and through with the great happiness that come from have do something for some one else .
`` It be nothing , '' he mutter .
`` It be a very great deal , '' reply Granny .
And then she change the subject .
`` How would you like to eat a dinner of Bowser the Hound 's ? ''
she ask .
CHAPTER XVII : Granny Fox Promises Reddy Bowser 's Dinner To give her child what each need To get the most from life he can , To work and play and live his best , Is wise Old Mother Nature 's plan .
-- Old Granny Fox .
Old Granny Fox ask Reddy how he would like to eat a dinner of Bowser the Hound 's , Reddy look at her sharply to see if she be joke or really mean what she say .
Granny look so sober and so much in earnest that Reddy decide she could n't be joke , even though it do sound that way .
`` I certainly would like it , Granny .
Yes , indeed , I certainly would like it , '' say he .
`` You -- you do n't suppose he will give u one , do you ? ''
Granny chuckle .
`` No , Reddy , '' say she .
`` Bowser be n't so generous a all that , especially to Foxes .
He be n't go to give u that dinner ; we be go to take it away from him .
Yes , Sir , we just naturally be go to take it away from , him . ''
Reddy do n't for the life of him see how it could be possible to take a dinner away from Bowser the Hound .
That seem to him almost as impossible a it be for him to climb or fly or dive .
But he have great faith in Granny 's cleverness .
He remember how she have so nearly caught Quacker the Duck .
He know that all the time he have be away try to find something for them to eat , old Granny Fox have be do more than just rest her tired old bone .
He know that not for one single minute have her sharp wit be idle .
He know that all that time she have be study and study to find some way by which they could get something to eat .
So great be his faith in Granny just then that if she have tell him she would get him a slice of the moon he would have believe her .
`` If you say we can take a dinner away from Bowser the Hound , I suppose we can , '' say Reddy , `` though I do n't see how .
But if we can , let 's do it right away .
I 'm hungry enough to dare almost anything for the sake of something to put in my stomach .
It be so empty that little bit of fish we divide be shake around a if it be lose .
Gracious , I could eat a million fish the size of that one !
Have you think of Fanner Brown 's hen , Granny ? ''
`` Of course , Reddy !
Of course !
What a silly question ! ''
replied Granny .
`` We may have to come to them yet . ''
`` I wish I be at them right now , '' interrupt Reddy with a sigh .
`` But you know what I have tell you , '' go on Granny .
`` The sure way of get into trouble be to steal hen .
I 'm not feel quite up to be chase by Bowser the Hound just now , and if we come right home we would give away the secret of where we live and might be smoke out , and that would be the end of u .
Besides , those hen will be hard to get this weather , because they will stay in their house , and there be no way for u to get in there unless we walk right in , in broad daylight , and that would never do .
It will be a great deal well to take Bowser 's dinner away from him .
In the first place , if we be careful , no one but Bowser will know about it , and as long a he be chain up , we will have nothing to worry about from him .
Besides , we will enjoy get even with him for the time he have spoil our chance of catch a fat chicken and for the way he have hunt u .

`` Just a you say , Granny ; just a you say , '' return Reddy .
`` You know best .
But how under the sun we can do it beat me . ''
`` It be very simple , '' reply Granny , `` very simple indeed .
Most thing be simple enough when you find out how to do them .
Neither of u could do it alone , but together we can do it without the least bit of risk .
Listen . ''
Granny go close to Reddy and whisper to him , although there be n't a soul within hearing .
A slow grin spread over Reddy 's face a he listen .
When she have finish , he laugh right out .
`` Granny , you be a wonder ! ''

Of course we can do it .
My , wo n't Bowser be surprise !
And how mad he 'll be !

CHAPTER XVIII : Why Bowser The Hound Did n't Eat His Dinner The thing you 've puzzle most about Is simple once you 've find it out .
-- Old Granny Fox .
Bowser The Hound dearly love to hunt just for the pleasure of the chase .
It be n't so much the desire to kill a it be the pleasure of use that wonderful nose of his and the excitement of try to catch some one , especially Granny or Reddy Fox .
Farmer Brown 's boy have put away his dreadful gun because he no longer want to kill the little people of the Green Forest and the Green Meadows , but rather to make them his friend .
Bowser have miss the exciting hunt he use to enjoy so much with Farmer Brown 's boy .
So Bowser have form the habit of slip away alone for a hunt every once in a while .
When Farmer Brown 's boy discover this , he get a chain and chain Bowser to his little house to keep him from run away and hunt on the sly .
Of course Bowser be n't keep chain all the time .
Oh , my , no !
When his master be about , where he could keep an eye on Bowser , he would let him go free .
But whenever he be go away and do n't want to take Bowser with him , he would chain Bowser up .
Now Bowser always have one good big meal a day .
To be sure , he have scrap or a bone now and then besides , but once a day he have one good big meal serve to him in a large tin pan .
If he happen to be chain , it be bring out to him .
If not , it be give to him just outside the kitchen door .
Granny Fox know all about this .
Sly old Granny make it her business to know the affair of other people around her because there be no tell when such knowledge may be of use to her .
So Granny have watch Bowser the Hound when he and his master have no idea at all that she be anywhere about , and she have find out his way , the usual hour for his dinner and just how far that chain would allow him to go .
It be such thing which she have store away in that shrewd old head of hers that make her so sure she and Reddy could take Bowser 's dinner away from him .
It be just about Bowser 's dinner-time when Granny and Reddy trot across the snow-covered field and crept behind the barn until they could peep around the corner .
No one be in sight , not even Bowser , who be inside his warm little house at the end of the long shed back of Farmer Brown 's house .
Granny saw that he be chain and a sly grin crept over her face .
`` You stay right here and watch until his dinner be bring out to him , '' say she to Reddy .
`` As soon a whoever bring it have go back to the house you walk right out where Bowser will see you .
At the sight of you , he 'll forget all about his dinner .
Sit right down where he can see you and stay there until you see that I have get that dinner , or until you hear somebody coming , for you know Bowser will make a great racket .
Then slip around back of the barn and join me back of that shed . ''
So Reddy sit down to watch , and Granny leave him .
By and by Mrs. Brown come out of the house with a pan full of good thing .
She put it down in front of Bowser 's little house and call to him .
Then she turn and hurry back , for it be very cold .
Bowser come out of his little house , yawn and stretch lazily .
It be time for Reddy to do his part .
Out he walk and sit down right in front of Bowser and grin at him .
Bowser star for a minute a if he doubt his own eye .
Such impudence !
Bowser growl .
Then with a yelp he spring towards Reddy .
Now the chain that hold him be long , but Reddy have take care not to get too near , and of course Bowser could n't reach him .
He tug with all his might and yelp and bark frantically , but Reddy just sit there and grin in the most provoking manner .
It be great fun to tease Bowser this way .
Meanwhile old Granny Fox have steal out from around the corner of the shed behind Bowser .
Getting hold of the edge of the pan with her teeth she pull it back with her around the corner and out of sight .
If she make any noise , Bowser do n't hear it .
He be make too much noise himself and be too excited .
Presently Reddy hear the sound of an opening door .
Mrs. Brown be come to see what all the fuss be about .
Like a flash Reddy dart behind the barn , and all Mrs. Brown saw be Bowser tug at his chain a he whine and yelp excitedly .
`` I guess he must have see a stray cat or something , '' say Mrs. Brown and go back in the house .
Bowser continue to whine and tug at his chain for a few minute .
Then he give it up and , growl deep in his throat , turn to eat his dinner .
But there be n't any dinner !
It have disappear , pan and all !
Bowser could n't understand it at all .
Back of the shed Granny and Reddy Fox lick that pan clean ; lick it until it be polish .
Then , with little sigh of satisfaction , and every once in a while a chuckle , they trot happily home .
CHAPTER XIX : Old Man Coyote Does A Little Thinking Investigate and for yourself find out Those thing which most you want to know about .
-- Old Granny Fox .
Never in all his life have Reddy Fox enjoy a dinner more than that one he and Granny have steal from Bowser the Hound .
Of course it would have taste delicious anyway , because they be so dreadfully hungry , but to Reddy it taste well still because it have be intend for Bowser .
Bowser have hunt Reddy so often that Reddy have no love for him at all , and it tickle him almost to death to think that they have take his dinner from almost under his nose .
With that good dinner in their stomach , Reddy and Granny Fox felt so much good that the Great World no longer seem such a cold and cruel place .
Funny how differently thing look when your stomach be full from the way those same thing look when it be empty .
Best of all they know they could play the same sharp trick again and steal another dinner from Bowser if need be .
It be a comfort feeling , a very comfort feeling , to know for a certainty where you can get another meal .
It be a feeling that Granny and Reddy Fox and many other little people of the Green Meadows and the Green Forest seldom have in winter .
As a rule , when they have eat one meal , they have n't the least idea where the next one be come from .
How would you like to live that way ?
The very next day Granny and Reddy go up to Farmer Brown 's at Bowser 's dinner hour .
But this time Farmer Brown 's boy be at work near the barn , and Bowser be not chain .
Granny and Reddy steal away as silently a they have come .
On the day follow they find Bowser chain and stole another dinner from him ; then they go away laugh until their side ache a they hear Bowser 's whine of surprise and disappointment when he discover that his dinner have vanish .
They know by the sound of his voice that he have n't the least idea what have become of that dinner .
Now there be some one else roam over the snow-covered meadow and through the Green Forest and the Old Pasture these day with a stomach so lean and empty that he could n't think of anything else .
It be Old Man Coyote .
You know he be very clever , be Old Man Coyote , and he manage to find enough food of one kind and another to keep him alive , but never enough to give him that comfortable feeling of a full stomach .
While he be n't actually starve , he be always hungry .
So he spend all the time when he be n't sleep in hunt for something to eat .
Of course he often run across the track of Granny and Reddy Fox , and once in a while he would meet them .
It strike Old Man Coyote that they do n't seem as thin a he be .
That set him to think .
Neither of them be a smarter hunter than he .
In fact , he pride himself on be smart than either of them .
Yet when he meet them , they seem to be in the best of spirit and not at all worried because food be so scarce .
Why ?
There must be a reason .
They must be get food of which he know nothing .
`` I 'll just keep an eye on them , '' mutter Old Man Coyote .
So very slyly and cleverly Old Man Coyote follow Granny and Reddy Fox , take the great care that they should not suspect that he be do it .
All one night he follow them through the Green Forest and over the Green Meadows , and when at last he saw them go home , appear not at all worry because they have catch nothing , he trot off to his own home to do some more thinking .
`` They be get food somewhere , that be sure , '' he mutter , a he scratch first one ear and then the other .
Somehow he could think good when he be scratch his ear .
`` If they do n't get it in the night , and they certainly do n't get anything this night , they must get it in the daytime .
I 've do considerable hunt myself in the daytime , and I have n't once meet them in the Green Forest or see them on the Green Meadows or up in the Old Pasture .
I wonder if they be steal Farmer Brown 's hen and have n't be find out yet .
I 've keep away from there myself , but if they can steal hen and not be catch , I certainly can .
There never be a Fox yet smart enough to do a thing that a Coyote can not do if he try .
I think I 'll slip up where I can watch Farmer Brown 's and see what be go on up there .
Yes , Sir , that 's what I 'll do . ''
With this , Old Man Coyote grin and then curl himself up for a short nap , for he be tire .
CHAPTER XX : A Twice Stolen Dinner No one ever be so smart that some one else may not prove to be smart still .
-- Old Granny Fox .
Listen and you shall hear all about three rogue .
Two be in red and be Granny and Reddy Fox .
And one be in gray and be Old Man Coyote .
They be the sly , smart rogue on all the Green Meadows or in all the Green Forest .
All three have start out to steal the same dinner , but the funny part be they do n't intend to steal it from the same person .
And still funny be it that one of them do n't even know where that dinner be or what kind of a dinner it would be .
True to his resolve to know what Granny and Reddy Fox be get to eat , and where they be get it , Old Man Coyote hid where he could see what be go on about Farmer Brown 's , for it be there he felt sure that Granny and Reddy be get food .
He have wait only a little while when along come Granny and Reddy Fox past the place where Old Man Coyote be hide .
They do n't see him .
Of course not .
He take care that they should have no chance .
But anyway , they be not think of him .
Their thought be all of that dinner they intend to have , and the smart trick by which they would get it .
So with their thought all on that dinner they slip up behind the barn and prepare to work the trick which have be so successful before .
Old Man Coyote crept after them .
He saw Reddy Fox lie down where he could peep around the corner of the barn to watch Bowser the Hound and to see that no one else be about .
He saw Granny leave Reddy there and hurry away .
Old Man Coyote 's wit work fast .
`` I ca n't be in two place at once , '' think he , `` so I ca n't watch both Granny and Reddy .
As I can watch but one , which one shall it be ?
Granny , of course .
Granny be the smartest of the two , and whatever they be up to , she be at the bottom of it .
Granny be the one to follow . ''
So , like a gray shadow , crafty Old Man Coyote stole after Granny Fox and saw her hide behind the corner of the shed at the end of which be the little house of Bowser the Hound .
He creep as near a he dare and then lay flat down behind a little bunch of dead grass close to the shed .
For some time nothing happen , and Old Man Coyote be puzzle .
Every once in a while Granny Fox would look behind and all about to be sure that no danger be near , but she do n't see Old Man Coyote .
After what seem to him a long time , he hear a door open on the other side of the shed .
It be Mrs. Brown carry Bowser 's dinner out to him .
Of course , Old Man Coyote do n't know this .
He know by the sound that some one have come out of the house , and it make him nervous .
He do n't like be so close to Farmer Brown 's house in broad daylight .
But he keep his eye on Granny Fox , and he saw her ear prick up in a way that he know meant that those sound be just what she have be wait for .
`` If she be n't afraid , I do n't need to be , '' think he craftily .
After a few minute he hear a door close and know that whoever have come out have go back into the house .
Almost at once Bowser the Hound begin to yelp and whine .
Swiftly Granny Fox disappear around the corner of the shed .
Just as swiftly Old Man Coyote run forward and peep around the corner .
There be Bowser the Hound tugging at his chain , and just beyond his reach be Reddy Fox , grin in the most provoking manner .
And there be Granny Fox , backing and dragging after her Bowser 's dinner .
In a flash Old Man Coyote understand the plan , and he almost chuckle aloud at the cleverness of it .
Then he hastily back behind the shed and wait .
In a minute Granny Fox appear , drag Bowser 's dinner .
She be so intent on get that dinner that she almost back into Old Man Coyote without suspect that he be anywhere about .
`` Thank you , Granny .
You need n't bother about it any longer ; I 'll take it now , '' growl Old Man Coyote in Granny 's ear .
Granny let go of that dinner a if it burn her tongue , and with a frightened little yelp leap to one side .
A minute later Reddy come race around from behind the barn eager for his share .
What he saw be Old Man Coyote bolt down that twice-stolen dinner while Granny Fox fairly dance with rage .
CHAPTER XXI : Granny And Reddy Talk Things Over .
You 'll find a on through life you go The thing you want may prove to be The very thing you should n't have .
Then seem loss be gain , you see .
-- Old Granny Fox .
If ever two folk be mad away through , those two be Granny and Reddy Fox a they watch Old Man Coyote gobble up the dinner they have so cleverly steal from Bowser the Hound .
It be bad enough to lose the dinner , but it be bad to see some one else eat it after they have work so hard to get it .
`` Robber ! ''
snarl Granny .
Old Man Coyote stop eat long enough to grin .
`` Thief !
Sneak !
Coward ! ''
snarl Reddy .
Once more Old Man Coyote grin .
When that dinner have disappear down his throat to the last and small crumb , he lick his chop and turn to Granny and Reddy .
`` I 'm very much oblige for that dinner , '' say he pleasantly , his eye twinkle with mischief .
`` It be the best dinner I have have for a long time .
Allow me to say that that trick of yours be a smart a trick a ever I have see .
It be quite worthy of a Coyote .
You be a very clever old lady , Granny Fox .
Now I hear some one coming , and I would suggest that it will be good for all concerned if we be not see about here . ''
He dart off behind the barn like a gray streak , and Granny and Reddy follow , for it be true that some one be come .
You see Bowser the Hound have discover that something be go on around the corner of the shed , and he make such a racket that Mrs. Brown have come out of the house to see what it be all about .
By the time she get around there , all she saw be the empty pan which have hold Bowser 's dinner .
She be puzzle .
How that pan could be where it be she could n't understand , and Bowser could n't tell her , although he try his very best .
She have be puzzle about that pan two or three time before .
Old Man Coyote lose no time in get back home , for he never felt easy near the home of man in broad daylight .
Granny and Reddy Fox go home too , and there be hate in their heart , -- hate for Old Man Coyote .
But once they reach home , Old Granny Fox stop growl , and presently she begin to chuckle .
`` What be you laugh at ? ''
demand Reddy .
`` At the way Old Man Coyote steal that dinner from u , '' reply Granny .
`` I hate him !
He 's a sneaking robber ! ''
snap Reddy .
`` Tut , tut , Reddy !
Tut , tut ! ''
retort Granny .
`` Be fair-minded .
We steal that dinner from Bowser the Hound , and Old Man Coyote steal it from u .
I guess he be no bad than we be , when you come to think it over .
Now be he ? ''
`` I -- I -- well , I do n't suppose he be , when you put it that way , '' Reddy admit grudgingly .
`` And he be smart , very smart , to outwit two such clever people a we be , '' continue Granny .
`` You will have to agree to that . ''
`` Y-e-s , '' say Reddy slowly .
`` He be smart enough , but -- '' `` There be n't any but , Reddy , '' interrupt Granny .
`` You know the law of the Green Meadows and the Green Forest .
It be everybody for himself , and anything belongs to one who have the wit or the strength to take it .
We have the wit to take that dinner from Bowser the Hound , and Old Man Coyote have the wit to take it from u and the strength to keep it .
It be all fair enough , and you know there be n't the least use in cry over spilled milk , a the saying be .
We simply have get to be smart enough not to let him fool u again .
I guess we wo n't get any more of Bowser 's dinner for a while .
We 've get to think of some other way of fill our stomach when the hunting be poor .
I think if I could have just one of those fat hen of Farmer Brown 's , it would put new strength into my old bone .
All summer I warn you to keep away from that henyard , but the time have come now when I think we might try for a couple of those hen . ''
Reddy prick up his ear at the mention of fat hen .
`` I think so too , '' say he .
`` When shall we try for one ? ''
`` To-morrow morning , '' reply Granny .
`` Now do n't bother me while I think out a plan . ''
CHAPTER XXII : Granny Fox Plans To Get A Fat Hen Full half success for Fox or Man Is win by work out a plan .
-- Old Granny Fox .
Granny Fox know this .
No one know it good .
Whatever she do be first carefully plan in her wise old head .
So now after she have decide that she and Reddy would try for one of Farmer Brown 's fat hen , she lay down to think out a plan to get that fat hen .
No one know good than she how foolish it would be to go over to that henyard and just trust to luck for a chance to catch one of those biddy .
Of course , they might be lucky and get a hen that way , but then again they might be unlucky and get in a peck of trouble .
`` You see , '' say she to Reddy , `` we must not only plan how to get that fat hen , but we must also plan how to get away with it safely .
If only there be some way of get in that henhouse at night , there would be no trouble at all .
I do n't suppose there be the least chance of that . ''
`` Not the least chance in the world , '' reply Reddy .
`` There be n't a hole anywhere big enough for even Shadow the Weasel to get through , and Farmer Brown 's boy be very careful to lock the door every night . ''
`` There 's a little hole that the hen go in and out of during the day , which be big enough for one of u to slip through , I believe , '' say Granny thoughtfully .
`` Sure !
But it 's always close at night , '' snap Reddy .
`` Besides , to get to that or the door either , you have get to get inside the henyard , and there 's a gate to that which we ca n't open . ''
`` People be sometimes careless , -- even you , Reddy , '' say Granny .
Reddy squirm uneasily , for he have be in trouble many time through carelessness .
`` Well , what of it ? ''
he demand a wee bit crossly .
`` Nothing much , only if that hen-yard gate should happen to be leave open , and if Farmer Brown 's boy should happen to forget to close that little hole that the hen go through , and if we happen to be around at just that time -- '' `` Too many ifs to get a dinner with , '' interrupt Reddy .
`` Perhaps , '' reply Granny mildly , `` but I 've notice that it be the one who have an eye open for all the little ifs in life that fare the best .
Now I 've keep an eye on that henyard , and I 've notice that very often Farmer Brown 's boy do n't close the henyard gate at night .
I suppose he think that if the henhouse door be lock , the gate do n't matter .
Any one who be careless about one thing , be likely to be careless about another .
Sometime he may forget to close that hole .
I tell you that we would try for one of those hen to-morrow morning , but the more I think about it , the more I think it will be wise to visit that henhouse a few night before we run the risk of try to catch a hen in broad daylight .
In fact , I be pretty sure I can make Farmer Brown 's boy forget to close that gate . ''
`` How ? ''
demand Reddy eagerly .
Granny grin .
`` I 'll try it first and tell you afterwards , '' say she .
`` I believe Farmer Brown 's boy close the henhouse up just before jolly , round , red Mr. Sun go to bed behind the Purple Hills , do n't he ? ''
Reddy nod .
Many time from a safe hiding-place he have hungrily watch Farmer Brown 's boy shut the biddy up .
It be always just before the Black Shadows begin to creep out from their hiding-places .
`` I think so , '' say Granny .
The truth be , she KNEW so .
There be nothing about that henhouse and what go on there that Granny do n't know quite as well a Reddy .
`` You stay right here this afternoon until I return .
I 'll see what I can do . ''
`` Let me go along , '' beg Reddy .
`` No , '' reply Granny in such a decided tone that Reddy know it would be of no use to tease .
`` Sometimes two can do what one can not do alone , and sometimes one can do what two might spoil .
Now we may as well take a nap until it be time for Mr. Sun to go to bed .
Just you leave it to your old Granny to take care of the first of those ifs .
For the other one we 'll have to trust to luck , but you know we be lucky sometimes . ''
With this Granny curl up for a nap , and have nothing well to do , Reddy follow her example .
CHAPTER XXIII : Farmer Brown 's Boy Forgets To Close The Gate How easy ' t be to just forget Until , ala , it be too late .
The most methodical of folk Sometimes forget to shut the gate .
-- Old Granny Fox .
Farmer Brown 's Boy be not usually the forgetful kind .
He be pretty good about not forget .
But Farmer Brown 's boy be n't perfect by any mean .
He do forget sometimes , and he be careless sometimes .
He would be a funny kind of boy otherwise .
But take it day in and day out , he be pretty thoughtful and careful .
The care of the hen be one of Farmer Brown 's boy 's duty .
It be one of those duty which most of the time be a pleasure .
He like the biddy , and he like to take care of them .
Every morning one of the first thing he do be to fee them and open the henhouse so that they can run in the henyard if they want to .
Every night he go out just before dark , collect the egg and lock the henhouse so that no harm can come to the biddy while they be asleep on their roost .
After the big snowstorm he have shovel a place in the henyard where the hen could come out and exercise and get a sun-bath when they want to , and in the very warm part of the clay they would do this .
Always in the daytime he take the great care to see that the henyard gate be fasten , for no one know good than he how bold Granny and Reddy Fox can be when they be very hungry , and in winter they be very apt to be very hungry most of the time .
So he do n't intend to give them a chance to slip into that henyard while the biddy be out , or to give the biddy a chance to stray outside where they might be still more easily catch .
But at night he sometimes leave that gate open , a Granny Fox have find out .
You see , he think it do n't matter because the hen be lock in their warm house and so be safe , anyway .
It be just at dusk of the afternoon of the day when Granny and Reddy Fox have talk over a plan to get one of those fat hen that Farmer Brown 's boy collect the egg and saw to it that the biddy have go to roost for the night .
He have just start to close the little sliding door across the hole through which the hen go in and out in the daytime when Bowser the Hound begin to make a great racket , a if terribly excite about something .
Farmer Brown 's boy give the little sliding door a hasty push , pick up his basket of egg , lock the henhouse door and hurry out through the gate without stop to close it .
You see , he be in a hurry to find out what Bowser be make such a fuss about .
Bowser be yelp and whine and tug at his chain , and it be plain to see that he be terribly eager to be set free .
`` What be it , Bowser , old boy ?
Did you see something ? ''
ask Farmer Brown 's boy a he pat Bowser on the head .
`` I ca n't let you go , you know , because you probably would go off hunt all night and come home in the morning all tire out and with sore foot .
Whatever it be , I guess you 've scar it out of a year 's growth , old fellow , so we 'll let it go at that . ''
Bowser still tug at his chain and whine , but after a little he quiet down .
His master look around behind the barn to see if he could see what have so stir up Bowser , but nothing be to be see , and he return , pat Bowser once more , and go into the house , never once give that open henyard gate another thought .
Half an hour later old Granny Fox join Reddy Fox , who be wait on the doorstep of their home .
`` It be all right , Reddy ; that gate be open , '' say she .
`` How do you do it , Granny ? ''
ask Reddy eagerly .
`` Easily enough , '' reply Granny .
`` I let Bowser get a glimpse of me just a his master be lock up the henhouse .
Bowser make a great fuss , and of course , Farmer Brown 's boy hurry out to see what it be all about .
He be in too much of a hurry to close that gate , and afterwards he forget all about it or else he think it do n't matter .
Of course , I do n't let him get so much a a glimpse of me . ''
`` Of course , '' say Reddy .
CHAPTER XXIV : A Midnight Visit By those who win ' t be well agree He 'll try and try who would succeed .
-- Old Granny Fox .
It seem to Reddy Fox a if time never have drag so slowly a it do this particular night while he and Granny Fox wait until Granny think it safe to visit Farmer Brown 's henhouse and see if by any chance there be a way of get into it .
Reddy try not to hope too much .
Granny have find a way to get the gate to the henyard leave open , but this would do them no good unless there be some way of get into the house , and this he very much doubt .
But if there be a way he want to know it , and he be impatient to start .
But Granny be in no hurry .
Not that she be n't just a hungry for a fat hen a be Reddy , but she be too wise and clever and altogether too sly to run any risk .
`` There be nothing gain by be in too much of a hurry , Reddy , '' say she , `` and often a great deal be lose in that way .
A fat hen will taste just as good a little later a it would now , and it will be foolish to go up to Farmer Brown 's until we be sure that everybody up there be asleep .
But to ease your mind , I 'll tell you what we will do ; we 'll go where we can see Farmer Brown 's house and watch until the last light wink out . ''
So they trot to a point where they could see Farmer Brown 's house , and there they sit down to watch .
It seem to Reddy that those light never would wink out .
But at last they do .
`` Come on , Granny ! ''
he cry , jump to his foot .
`` Not yet , Reddy .
Not yet , '' reply Granny .
`` We 've get to give folk time to get sound asleep .
If we should get into that henhouse , those hen might make a racket , and if anything like that be go to happen , we want to be sure that Farmer Brown and Farmer Brown 's boy be asleep . ''
This be sound advice , and Reddy know it .
So with a groan he once more threw himself down on the snow to wait .
At last Granny arise , stretch , and look up at the twinkle star .
`` Come on , '' say she and lead the way .
Up back of the barn and around it they steal like two shadow and quite as noiselessly a shadow .
They hear Bowser the Hound sighing in his sleep in his snug little house , and grin at each other .
Silently they steal over to the henyard .
The gate be open , just a Granny have tell Reddy it would be .
Across the henyard they trot swiftly , straight to where more than once in the daytime they have see the hen come out of the house through a little hole .
It be close .
Reddy have expect it would be .
Still , he be dreadfully disappointed .
He give it merely a glance .
`` I know it would n't be any use , '' say he with a half whine .
But Granny pay no attention to him .
She go close to the hole and push gently against the little door that close it .
It do n't move .
Then she notice that at one edge there be a tiny crack .
She try to push her nose through , but the crack be too narrow .
Then she try a paw .
A claw caught on the edge of the door , and it move ever so little .
Then Granny know that the little door be n't fasten .
Granny stretch herself flat on the ground and go to work , first with one paw , then with the other .
By and by she catch her claw in it just right again , and it move a wee bit more .
No , most certainly that door be n't fasten , and that crack be a little wider .
`` What be you waste your time there for ? ''
demand Reddy crossly .
`` We 'd well be off hunt if we would have anything to eat this night . ''
Granny say nothing but keep on work .
She have discover that this be a sliding door .
Presently the crack be wide enough for her to get her nose in .
Then she push and twist her head this way and that .
The little door slowly slide back , and when Reddy turn to speak to her again , for he have have his back to her , she be nowhere to be see .
Reddy just gap and gap foolishly .
There be no Granny Fox , but there be a black hole where she have be work , and from it come the most delicious smell , -- the smell of fat hen !
It seem to Reddy that his stomach fairly flop over with longing .
He rub his eye to be sure that he be awake .
Then in a twinkling he be inside that hole himself .
`` Sh-h-h , be still ! ''
whisper Old Granny Fox .
CHAPTER XXV : A Dinner For Two Dark deed be do in the stilly night , And who shall say if they 're wrong or right ?
-- Old Granny Fox .
It all depend on how you look at thing .
Of course , Granny and Reddy Fox have no business to be in Farmer Brown 's henhouse in the middle of the night , or at any other time , for that matter .
That be , they have no business to be there , a Farmer Brown would look at the matter .
He would have call them two red thief .
Perhaps that be just what they be .
But look at the matter a they do , I be not so sure about it .
To Granny and Reddy Fox those hen be simply big , rather stupid bird , splendid eat if they could be catch , and bound to be eat by somebody .
The fact that they be in Farmer Brown 's henhouse do n't make them his any more than the fact that Mrs. Grouse be in a part of the Green Forest own by Farmer Brown make her his .
You see , among the little meadow and forest people there be no such thing a property right , except in the matter of storehouse , and because these hen be alive , it do n't occur to Granny and Reddy that the henhouse be a sort of storehouse .
It would have make no difference if it have .
Among the little people it be consider quite right to help yourself from another 's storehouse if you be smart enough to find it and really need the food .
Besides , Reddy and Granny know that Fanner Brown and his boy would eat some of those hen themselves , and they do n't begin to need them a Reddy and Granny do .
So a they look at the matter , there be nothing wrong in be in that henhouse in the middle of the night .
They be there simply because they need food very , very much , and food be there .
They star up at the roost where the biddy be huddle together , fast asleep .
They be too high up to be reach from the floor even when Reddy and Granny stand on their hind leg and stretch as far a they could .
`` We 've get to wake them up and scare them so that some of the silly thing will fly down where we can catch them , '' say Reddy , lick his lip hungrily .
`` That wo n't do at all ! ''
snap Granny .
`` They would make a great racket and waken Bowser the Hound , and he would waken his master , and that be just what we must n't do if we hope to ever get in here again .
I think you have more sense , Reddy . ''
Reddy look a little shamefaced .
`` Well , if we do n't do that , how be we go to get them ?
We ca n't fly , '' he grumble .
`` You stay right here where you be , '' snap Granny , `` and take care that you do n't make a sound . ''
Then Granny jump lightly to a little shelf that run along in front of the nesting box .
From this she could reach the low roost on which four fat hen be asleep .
Very gently she push her head in between two of these and crowd them apart .
Sleepily they protest and move along a little .
Granny continue to crowd them .
At last one of them stretch out her head to see who be crowd so .
Like a flash Granny seize that head , and biddy never know what have waken her , nor do she have a chance to waken the others .
Dropping this hen at Reddy 's foot , Granny crowd another until she do the same thing , and just the same thing happen once more .
Then Granny jump lightly down , pick up one of the hen by the neck , sling the body over her shoulder , and tell Reddy to do the same with the other and start for home .
`` Are n't you go to get any more while we have the chance ? ''
grumble Reddy .
`` Enough be enough , '' retort Granny .
`` We 've get a dinner for two , and so far no one be any the wiser .
Perhaps these two wo n't be miss , and we 'll have a chance to get some more another night .
Now come on . ''
This be plain common sense , and Reddy know it , so without another word he follow old Granny Fox out by the way they have enter , and then home to the best dinner he have have for a long long time .
CHAPTER XXVI : Farmer Brown 's Boy Sets A Trap The trouble be that trouble be , More frequently than not , Brought on by naught but carelessness ; By some one who forget .
-- Old Granny Fox .
Granny Fox have hop that those two hen she and Reddy have steal from Farmer Brown 's henhouse would not be miss , but they be .
They be miss the very first thing the next morning when Farmer Brown 's boy go to fee the biddy .
He discover right away that the little sliding door which should have close the opening through which the hen go in and out of the house be open , and then he remember that he have leave the henyard gate open the night before .
Carefully Farmer Brown 's boy examine the hole with the slide door .
`` Ha ! ''
say he presently , and hold up two red hair which he have find on the edge of the door .
`` Ha !
I think as much .
I be careless last night and do n't fasten this door , and I leave the gate open .
Reddy Fox have be here , and now I know what have become of those two hen .
I suppose it serve me right for my carelessness , and I suppose if the truth be know , those hen be of more real good to him than they ever could have be to me , because the poor fellow must be have pretty hard work to get a living these hard winter day .
Still , I ca n't have him steal any more .
That would never do at all .
If I shut them up every night and be not careless , he ca n't get them .
But accident will happen , and I might do just a I do last night -- think I have lock up when I have n't .
I do n't like to set a trap for Reddy , but I must teach the rascal a lesson .
If I do n't , he will get so bold that those chicken wo n't be safe even in broad daylight . ''
Now at just that very time over in their home , Granny and Reddy Fox be talk over plan for the future , and shrewd old Granny be point out to Reddy how necessary it be that they should keep away from that henyard for some time .
`` We 've have a good dinner , a splendid dinner , and if we be smart enough we may be able to get more good dinner where this one come from , '' say she .
`` But we certainly wo n't if we be too greedy . ''
`` But I do n't believe Farmer Brown 's boy have miss those two chicken , and I do n't see any reason at all why we should n't go back there to-night and get two more if he be stupid enough to leave that gate and little door open , '' whine Reddy .
`` Maybe he have n't miss those two , but if we should take two more he certainly would miss them , and he would guess what have become of them , and that might get u into no end of trouble , '' snap Granny .
`` We be not starve now , and the best thing for u to do be to keep away from that henhouse until we ca n't get anything to eat anywhere else , Now you mind what I tell you , Reddy , and do n't you dare go near there . ''
Reddy promise , and so it come about that Farmer Brown 's boy hunt up a trap all for nothing so far a Reddy and Granny be concern .
Very carefully he bind strip of cloth around the jaw of the trap , for he could n't bear to think of those cruel jaw cut into the leg of Reddy , should he happen to get caught .
You see , Farmer Brown 's boy do n't intend to kill Reddy if he should catch him , but to make him a prisoner for a while and so keep him out of mischief .
That night he hide the trap very cunningly just inside the henhouse where any one creeping through that little hole make for the hen to go in and out would be sure to step in it .
Then he purposely leave the little sliding door open part way a if it have be forget , and he also leave the henyard gate open just a he have do the night before .
`` There now , Master Reddy , '' say he , talk to himself , `` I rather think that you be go to get into trouble before morning . ''
And doubtless Reddy would have do just that thing but for the wisdom of sly old Granny .
CHAPTER XXVII : Prickly Porky Takes A Sun Bath Danger come when least expect ; ' T be often near when not expect .
-- Old Granny Fox .
The long hard winter have pass , and Spring have come .
Prickly Porky the Porcupine come down from a tall poplar-tree and slowly stretch himself .
He be tire of eating .
He be tire of swing in the tree-top .
`` I believe I 'll have a sun-bath , '' say Prickly Porky , and lazily walk toward the edge of the Green Forest in search of a place where the sun lay warm and bright .
Now Prickly Porky 's stomach be very , very full .
He be fat and naturally lazy , so when he come to the doorstep of an old house just on the edge of the Green Forest he sit down to rest .
It be sunny and warm there , and the longer he sit the less like move he felt .
He look about him with his dull eye and grunt to himself .
`` It 's a deserted house .
Nobody live here , and I guess nobody 'll care if I take a nap right here on the doorstep , '' say Prickly Porky to himself .
`` And I do n't care if they do , '' he add , for Prickly Porky the Porcupine be afraid of nobody and nothing .
So Prickly Porky make himself as comfortable a possible , yawned once or twice , try to wink at jolly , round , red Mr. Sun , who be wink and smile down at him and then fell fast asleep right on the doorstep of the old house .
Now the old house have be desert .
No one have live in it for a long , long time , a very long time indeed .
But it happen that , the night before , old Granny Fox and Reddy Fox have have to move out of their nice home on the edge of the Green Meadows because Farmer Brown 's boy have find it .
Reddy be very stiff and sore , for he have be shoot by a hunter .
He be so sore he could hardly walk , and could not go very far .
So old Granny Fox have lead him to the old desert house and put him to bed in that .
`` No one will think of look for u here , for every one know that no one live here , '' say old Granny Fox , a she make Reddy as comfortable a possible .
As soon a it be daylight , Granny Fox slip out to watch for Farmer Brown 's boy , for she felt sure that he would come back to the house they have leave , and sure enough he do .
He bring a spade and dig the house open , and all the time old Granny Fox be watch him from behind a fence corner and laugh to think that she have be smart enough to move in the night .
But Reddy Fox do n't know anything about this .
He be so tired that he sleep and sleep and sleep .
It be the middle of the morning when finally he awake .
He yawn and stretch , and when he stretch he groan because he be so stiff and sore .
Then he hobble up toward the doorway to see if old Granny Fox have leave any breakfast outside for him .
It be dark , very dark .
Reddy be puzzle .
Could it be that he have get up before daylight -- that he have n't sleep as long a he think ?
Perhaps he have sleep the whole day through , and it be night again .
My , how hungry he be !
`` I hope Granny have catch a fine , fat chicken for me , '' think Reddy , and his mouth water .
Just then he run bump into something .
`` Wow ! ''
scream Reddy Fox , and clap both hand to his nose .
Something be stick into it .
It be one of the sharp little spear that Prickly Porky hide in his coat .
Reddy Fox know then why the old house be so dark .
Prickly Porky be block up the doorway .
CHAPTER XXVIII : Prickly Porky Enjoys Himself A boasting tongue , as sure a fate , Will trip it owner soon or late .
-- Old Granny Fox .
Prickly Porky the Porcupine be enjoy himself .
There be no doubt about that .
He be stretch across the doorway of that old house , the very house in which old Granny Fox have be bear .
When he have lie down on the doorstep for a nap and sun-bath , he have think that the old house be still desert .
Then he have fall asleep , only to be waken by Reddy Fox , who bad be asleep in the old house and who could n't get out because Prickly Porky be in the way .
Now Prickly Porky do not love Reddy Fox , and the more Reddy beg and scold and call him names , the more Prickly Porky chuckle .
It be such a good joke to think that he have trap Reddy Fox , and he make up his mind that he would keep Reddy in there a long time just to tease him and make him uncomfortable .
You see Prickly Porky remember how often Reddy Fox play mean trick on little meadow and forest folk who be small and weak than himself .
`` It will do him good .
It certainly will do him good , '' say Prickly Porky , and rattle the thousand little spear hide in his long coat , for he know that the very sound of them would make Reddy Fox shiver with fright .
Suddenly Prickly Porky prick up his funny little short ear .
He hear the deep voice of Bowser the Hound , and it be come nearer and nearer .
Prickly Porky chuckle again .
`` I guess Mr. Bowser be go to have a surprise ; I certainly think he be , '' say Prickly Porky a he make all the thousand little spear stand out from his long coat till he look like a funny great chestnut burr .
Bowser the Hound do have a surprise .
He be hunt Reddy Fox , and he almost run into Prickly Porky before he saw him .
The very sight of those thousand little spear send little cold chill chase each other down Bowser 's backbone clear to the tip of his tail , for he remember how he have get some of them in his lip and mouth once upon a time , and how it have hurt to have them pull out .
Ever since then he have have the great respect for Prickly Porky .
`` Wow ! ''
yelp Bowser the Hound , stop short .
`` I beg your pardon , Prickly Porky , I beg your pardon , I do n't know you be take a nap here . ''
All the time Bowser the Hound be back away as fast a he could .
Then he turn around , put his tail between his leg and actually run away .
Slowly Prickly Porky unroll , and his little eye twinkle a he watch Bowser the Hound run away .
`` Bowser 's very big and strong ; His voice be deep ; his leg be long ; His bark scar some almost to death .
But a for me he waste his breath ; I just roll up and shake my spear And Bowser be the one who fear . ''
So say Prickly Porky , and laugh aloud .
Just then he hear a light footstep and turn to see who be come .
It be old Granny Fox .
She have see Bowser run away , and now she be anxious to find out if Reddy Fox be safe .
`` Good morning , '' say Granny Fox , take care not to come too near .
`` Good morning , '' reply Prickly Porky , hide a smile .
`` I 'm very tired and would like to go inside my house ; have you just a soon move ? ''
ask Granny Fox .
`` Oh ! ''
exclaim Prickly Porky , `` be this your house ?
I think you live over on the Green Meadows . ''
`` I do , but I 've move .
Please let me in , '' reply Granny Fox .
`` Certainly , certainly .
Do n't mind me , Granny Fox .
Step right over me , '' say Prickly Porky , and smile once more , and at the same time rattle his little spear .
Instead of step over him , Granny Fox back away .
CHAPTER XXIX : The New Home In The Old Pasture Who keep a watch upon his toe Need never fear he 'll bump his nose .
-- Old Granny Fox .
Now there be nothing like be shut in alone in the dark to make one think .
A voice inside of Reddy begin to whisper to him .
`` If you have n't try to be smart and show off you would n't have bring all this trouble on yourself and Old Granny Fox , '' say the voice .
`` I know it , '' reply Reddy right out loud , forget that it be only a small voice inside of him .
`` What do you know ? ''
ask Prickly Porky .
He be still keep Reddy in and Granny out and he have overheard what Reddy say .
`` It be none of your business ! ''
snap Reddy .
Reddy could hear Prickly Porky chuckle .
Then Prickly Porky repeat a if to himself in a queer crack voice the following : `` Rudeness never , never pay , Nor be there gain in saucy way .
It 's always best to be polite And ne'er give way to ugly spite .
If that 's the way you feel inside You 'd better all such feeling hide ; For he must smile who hop to win , And he who lose best will grin . ''
Reddy pretend that he have n't hear .
Prickly Porky continue to chuckle for a while and finally Reddy fell asleep .
When he awake it be to find that Prickly Porky have leave and old Granny Fox have bring him something to eat .
Just as soon a Reddy Fox be able to travel he and Granny have move to the Old Pasture .
The Old Pasture be very different from the Green Meadows or the Green Forest .
Yes , indeed , it be very , very different .
Reddy Fox think so .
And Reddy do n't like the change , -- not a bit .
All about be great rock , and around and over them grow bush and young tree and bull-briars with long ugly thorn , and blackberry and raspberry cane that seem to have a million little hooked hand , reach to catch in and tear his red coat and to scratch his face and hand .
There be little open place where wild-eyed young cattle feed on the short grass .
They have make many little path all crisscross among the bush , and when you try to follow one of these path you never could tell where you be come out .
No , Reddy Fox do not like the Old Pasture at all .
There be no long , soft green grass to lie down in .
And it be lonesome up there .
He miss the little people of the Green Meadows and the Green Forest .
There be no one to bully and tease .
And it be such a long , long way from Farmer Brown 's henyard that old Granny Fox would n't even try to bring him a fat hen .
At least , that 's what she tell Reddy .
The truth be , wise old Granny Fox know that the very best thing she could do be to stay away from Farmer Brown 's for a long time .
She know that Reddy could n't go down there , because he be still too lame and sore to travel such a long way , and she hop that by the time Reddy be well enough to go , he would have learn good than to do such a foolish thing a to try to show off by steal a chicken in broad daylight , a he have when he bring all this trouble on them .
Down on the Green Meadows , the home of Granny and Reddy Fox have be on a little knoll , which you know be a little low hill , right where they could sit on their doorstep and look all over the Green Meadows .
It have be very , very beautiful down there .
They have make lovely little path through the tall green meadow grass , and the buttercup and daisy have grow close up to their very doorstep .
But up here in the Old Pasture Granny Fox have choose the thick clump of bush and young tree she could find , and in the middle be a great pile of rock .
Way in among these rock Granny Fox have dig their new house .
It be right down under the rock .
Even in the middle of the day jolly , round , red Mr. Sun could hardly find it with a few of his long , bright beam .
All the rest of the time it be dark and gloomy there .
No , Reddy Fox do n't like his new home at all , but when he say so old Granny Fox box his ear .
`` It 's your own fault that we 've get to live here now , '' say she .
`` It 's the only place where we be safe .
Farmer Brown 's boy never will find this home , and even if he do he could n't dig into it a he do into our old home on the Green Meadows .
Here we be , and here we 've get to stay , all because a foolish little Fox think himself smart than anybody else and try to show off . ''
Reddy hang his head .
`` I do n't care ! ''
he say , which be very , very foolish , because , you know , he do care a very great deal .
And here we will leave wise Old Granny Fox and Reddy , safe , even if they do not like their new home .
You see , Lightfoot the Deer be get jealous .
He think there should be some book about the people of the Green Forest , and that the first one should be about him .

CHAPTER I. MRS. REDWING 'S SPECKLED EGG Old Mother West Wind come down from the Purple Hills in the golden light of the early morning .
Over her shoulder be sling a bag -- a great big bag -- and in the bag be all of Old Mother West Wind 's child , the Merry Little Breezes .
Old Mother West Wind come down from the Purple Hills to the Green Meadows and a she walk she croon a song : `` Ships upon the ocean wait ; I must hurry , hurry on !
Mills be idle if I 'm late ; I must hurry , hurry on . ''
When she reach the Green Meadows Old Mother West Wind open her bag , turn it upside down and shake it .
Out tumble all the Merry Little Breezes and begin to spin round and round for very joy , for you see they be to lay in the Green Meadows all day long until Old Mother West Wind should come back at night and take them all to their home behind the Purple Hills .
First they race over to see Johnny Chuck .
They find Johnny Chuck sit just outside his door eat his breakfast .
One , for very mischief , snatch right out of Johnny Chuck 's mouth the green leaf of corn he be eat , and run away with it .
Another playfully pull his whisker , while a third rumple up his hair .
Johnny Chuck pretend to be very cross indeed , but really he do n't mind a bit , for Johnny Chuck love the Merry Little Breezes and play with them everyday .
And if they tease Johnny Chuck they be good to him , too .
When they saw Farmer Brown come across the Green Meadows with a gun one of them would dance over to Johnny Chuck and whisper to him that Farmer Brown be come , and then Johnny Chuck would hide away , deep down in his snug little house under ground , and Farmer Brown would wonder and wonder why it be that he never , never could get near enough to shoot Johnny Chuck .
But he never , never could .
When the Merry Little Breezes leave Johnny Chuck they race across the Green Meadows to the Smiling Pool to say good morning to Grandfather Frog who sit on a big lily pad watch for green fly for breakfast .
`` Chug-arum , '' say Grandfather Frog , which be his way of say good morning .
Just then along come a fat green fly and up jump Grandfather Frog .
When he sit down again on the lily pad the fat green fly be nowhere to be see , but Grandfather Frog look very well satisfied indeed a he contentedly rub his white waistcoat with one hand .
`` What be the news , Grandfather Frog ? ''
cry the Merry Little Breezes .
`` Mrs. Redwing have a new speckled egg in her nest in the bulrush , '' say Grandfather Frog .
`` We must see it , '' cry the Merry Little Breezes , and away they all run to the swamp where the bulrush grow .
Now someone else have hear of Mrs. Redwing 's dear little nest in the bulrush , and he have start out bright and early that morning to try and find it , for he want to steal the little speckled egg just because they be pretty .
It be Tommy Brown , the farmer 's boy .
When the Merry Little Breezes reach the swamp where the bulrush grow they find poor Mrs. Redwing in great distress .
She be afraid that Tommy Brown would find her dear little nest , for he be very , very near it , and his eye be very , very sharp .
`` Oh , '' cry the Merry Little Breezes , `` we must help Mrs. Redwing save her pretty speckle egg from bad Tommy Brown ! ''
So one of the Merry Little Breezes whisk Tommy Brown 's old straw hat off his head over into the Green Meadows .
Of course Tommy ran after it .
Just a he stoop to pick it up another little Breeze run away with it .
Then they take turn , first one little Breeze , then another little Breeze run away with the old straw hat just a Tommy Brown would almost get his hand on it .
Down past the Smiling Pool and across the Laughing Brook they race and chase the old straw hat , Tommy Brown run after it , very cross , very red in the face , and breathe very hard .
Way across the Green Meadows they run to the edge of the wood , where they hang the old straw hat in the middle of a thorn tree .
